=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
It took me years to get Brass to the table. I had heard it was a nightmare of exception based rules and mechanics that worked one way in one phase and then differently in another. I glanced at the rulebook and that certainly seemed to be the case. Eventually, I made myself sit down, focus up and read up on it.

As I took it in, slowly and deliberately, I realized that the game is rather simple. Play a card, do a thing in that area. The possible actions numbered only five and even those were fairly rules light. I went through the "exceptions" that I had heard so much about and suddenly I realized that once you knew how the game worked, those exceptions were sort of obvious. It was just clumsy writing to explain certain spots on the map that would seem confusing had you never played before.

"This will be a piece of cake", I thought. Then I sat down to explain it. Suddenly, it felt like the exceptions had tripled. The easy feeling action menu suddenly had much more depth than I was able to explain. I found myself saying "Oh, and one more thing..." every five minutes. The criticisms are true, this game is a mess of caveats.

Still, as clumsy as that first game felt, once you get going it is one of the smoothest games you'll ever play. Caveats aside, the actions are simple and brief. The game flies along once everyone knows what they are doing. The strategies are quite deep as well, do you build a verticle organization that hoards all the points for yourself at great expense or do you try and piggyback on what others are doing, simply providing them the tools to score points, so you can too?

The scoring system reminds me quite a bit of Wallace's legendary train games, as more points equal more money, but ultimately the money is worthless. It only matters how much you have built and how efficiently you did it. I have barely scratched the surface of this one, but I have a strong feeling it is going to be one of my favorites for a long, long, time.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
Really good game.  Someone in the forums compared it with Power Grid, and I agree.  Brass does seem to fit a similar spot in the game spectrum as Power Grid.  While I generally love most of Martin Wallace's games, many of them are a little too deep to get regular play.  This one will probably get pulled out often, as it has the depth of Wallace's great games, but a level of play a notch below his other more difficult games. I'd recommend having someone teach you this one.

Economic sim. We are budding industrialists seeking fortune by exporting cotton from our mills.  Paths to profit are diverse by investing in coal mining, iron plants, ship ports, and laying networks of canal in the early phase or rail at the end. Cards are used for development and for tile placing. Pretty smooth, meaty strategy decisions with limited resources and development locations.  Late game rounds mushroom into big scoring plays. Long.

RATING: 7
purchased April Fools '08. Have played two games in quick succession May 08, both 4 player. An intriguing game where  you certainly need to maintain a flexibility with your hand as other players interfere with your plans. This ability to change plans and maneuver reduce significantly as your hand depletes later in each era. Also turn order plays a *huge* part enabling you to set up and then smash your *serve* before other players beat you to the quick. Then there's the wide range of strategies that are open in the game, it sometimes can be a little mind boggling, which I think is the games best and yet biggest flaw. Players are left gaping with possibilities, and often will end up paralysing over it. Admittedly though the second game felt easier as far as playing the mechanics, but we still took 4 hrs to play the game! Still, this is another Wallace game I'm rather smitten like a kitten with. It's right up there with Aos and struggle. Look forward to more games...
Update: Long time since I've played this puppy. One thing that tripped me was what defined your 'Network' and where you can play cards to to build, and also how you acquire coal to build. I'd recommend rereading these subtleties if you haven't played for a while and need a refresher.

RATING: 7
I've played numerous times, now (thankfully) by the correct rules.  Great game!  Ship-building is definitely not a game-breaking strategy.

Players are confronted with multiple decisions each turn (build rails? build an industry? ship cotton? take a loan? research?) - all of them interesting.

Brass is as good as Perikles, which I rank as one of Wallace's better recent efforts.

[i]Update:[/i]

I prefer Age of Industry to Brass, due to the lower fiddly factor, support for an extra player, multiple board expansions, and various rules revisions.  Brass is now on the trade pile.

Wow. Much easier to play than I thought it would be. Various paths to victory.   A wonderful economic game. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Played twice (with 3 and 4 players). The rules are a bit confusing (we made at least one minor mistake in each game). Lots of interesting ideas in this game, which work rather well overall - but some of them really add a lot of rules for a very little game effect, and I suspect the game would have gained a lot (at least for me) if some of these small rules had been streamlined a bit. However, my major gripe is the randomness of the card draw, especially since you have no visibility of the cards you will get at the beginning of the rail period, and thus cannot start preparing your strategy in that direction at the end of the canal period. Of course, experience probably helps with that (but even then, I am worried that getting a "good" draw will still be a large advantage). I will definitely try and play it again, but I fear that the cards will prevent me from really liking this game.

RATING: 8
Steep learning curve. Ability to keep many small details in player's mind required. In Brass you build networks and the smallish playing area quickly evolves into a complex system. For a newbie, it's next to impossible to see who's actually winning, until you tally the final score. Amazingly underwhelming art and visuals. Rewards patience, but all the abstraction distances the game from its thematic, real world elements. However, experience reveals a deep and very satisfying gaming experience.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This game really is a blast: definitely in the league of Age of Steam. It is not that unforgiving but mostly because the player interaction can help you out when you made a mistake. Very good mix of cooperative and competitive play.
At first the board seems static but every game plays different enough from each other. Fast turns ensure a low downtime while every decision you make will still highly influence your position on the board and the outcome of the game.
This game offers really a lot: technical development, transportation and logistics optimization, cooperative work, a market simulation, risk management... Martin Wallace has proven to be a high calibre game designer that puts out hit after hit!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
As of yet Brass is the best game I have ever played. It took me 2 or 3 games before I fully understood what was going on and even now after 12 or so plays I feel like I still have a lot to learn about the game. I would play this game so much more if only I could find people to play it with... Still it stands as my favorite game of all time and I truly savor every chance I get to play. Mr. Wallace you are a master.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
经济类游戏中的最佳作品，背景选材，和游戏体验结合的非常到位;设计师马丁最硬派的作品之一。游戏中玩家需要打出卡牌，在（建设，升级，贷款，网络，出售）中选择需要执行的行动，游戏获胜的方式非常多，几乎没有最优的路线。此外BRASS在本人眼中也相当于一块试金石，一局下来可以用来区分鉴定中度到重度玩家这两个领域。
【关键词】运河/铁路时期，合并万能行动，利物浦造船厂，远洋阿三市场，金环链接记分，算子翻面记分，建筑升级，市场供求，煤/钢运输区别，终盘贷款限制

【推荐度】极高  【网络经济，中重度德式爱好者

Maybe some people do like this game because of this fact that winning process is hard to be found ant if you can accept this fact as replayability in positive way, maybe you'll like this game.
